\n247: Without ADS, the CDS/EDS/RDS streams may point at distinct management servers,\n248: or when on the same management server at distinct gRPC streams/connections that\n249: require coordination. Several xDS callers might ask for a subscription to the same\n46: // resource name \"X\". The xDS machinery must return to each their very own subscription to X.\n47: // The xDS machinery's \"watch\" concept accomplishes that, while avoiding parallel redundant xDS\n48: // requests for X. Each of those subscriptions is viewed as a \"watch\" on X, while behind the scenes\n49: // there is just a single real subscription to that resource name.\n50: //\n51: // This class maintains the watches<-->subscription mapping: it\n52: // 1) delivers updates to all interested watches, and\n53: // 2) tracks which resource names should be {added to,removed from} the subscription when the\n54: //    {first,last} watch on a resource name is {added,removed}.\n55: //\n56: // #1 is accomplished by WatchMap's implementation of the SubscriptionCallbacks interface.\n57: // This interface allows the xDS client to just throw each xDS update message it receives directly\n58: // into WatchMap::onConfigUpdate, rather than having to track the various watches' callbacks.\n59: //\n60: // The information for #2 is returned by updateWatchInterest(); the caller should use it to\n61: // update the subscription accordingly.\n62: //\n63: // A WatchMap is assumed to be dedicated to a single type_url type of resource (EDS, CDS, etc).\n64: //\n65: // The WatchMap can also store the fetched resources in a cache, and allow others to fetch\n66: // resources directly from the cache. This is done for EDS in the following case:\n67: // Assume an active EDS cluster exists with some load-assignment that is kept in the cache.\n68: // If the cluster is updated, and no load-assignment is sent from the xDS server, the\n69: // cached version will be used.\n70: // The WatchMap is responsible to update the cache with the resource contents, and it is\n71: // up to the specific xDS type subscription handler (i.e., EdsClusterImpl), to fetch\n72: // the resource from the cache.\n73: class WatchMap : public UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks, public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\n74: public:\n75:   WatchMap(const bool use_namespace_matching, const std::string& type_url,\n76:            CustomConfigValidators* config_validators, EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache)\n77:       : use_namespace_matching_(use_namespace_matching), type_url_(type_url),\n78:         config_validators_(config_validators), eds_resources_cache_(eds_resources_cache) {\n79:     // If eds resources cache is provided, then the type must be ClusterLoadAssignment.\n80:     ASSERT(!eds_resources_cache_.has_value() ||\n81:            (type_url == Config::getTypeUrl<envoy::config::endpoint::v3::ClusterLoadAssignment>()));\n82:   }\n83: \n84:   // Adds 'callbacks' to the WatchMap, with every possible resource being watched.\n85:   // (Use updateWatchInterest() to narrow it down to some specific names).\n86:   // Returns the newly added watch, to be used with updateWatchInterest and removeWatch.\n87:   Watch* addWatch(SubscriptionCallbacks& callbacks, OpaqueResourceDecoder& resource_decoder);\n88: \n89:   // Updates the set of resource names that the given watch should watch.\n90:   // Returns any resource name additions/removals that are unique across all watches. That is:\n91:   // 1) if 'resources' contains X and no other watch cares about X, X will be in added_.\n92:   // 2) if 'resources' does not contain Y, and this watch was the only one that cared about Y,\n93:   //    Y will be in removed_.\n94:   AddedRemoved updateWatchInterest(Watch* watch,\n95:                                    const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& update_to_these_names);\n96: \n97:   // Expects that the watch to be removed has already had all of its resource names removed via\n98:   // updateWatchInterest().\n99:   void removeWatch(Watch* watch);\n100: \n101:   // UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks.\n102:   void onConfigUpdate(const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<Protobuf::Any>& resources,\n103:                       const std::string& version_info) override;\n104: \n105:   void onConfigUpdate(const std::vector<DecodedResourcePtr>& resources,\n106:                       const std::string& version_info) override;\n107: \n108:   void\n109:   onConfigUpdate(absl::Span<const envoy::service::discovery::v3::Resource* const> added_resources,\n110:                  const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<std::string>& removed_resources,\n111:                  const std::string& system_version_info) override;\n112:   void onConfigUpdateFailed(ConfigUpdateFailureReason reason, const EnvoyException* e) override;\n113: \n114:   WatchMap(const WatchMap&) = delete;\n115:   WatchMap& operator=(const WatchMap&) = delete;\n116: \n117:   void setConfigValidators(CustomConfigValidators* config_validators) {\n118:     config_validators_ = config_validators;\n119:   }\n120: \n121: private:\n122:   void removeDeferredWatches();\n123: \n124:   // Given a list of names that are new to an individual watch, returns those names that are in fact\n125:   // new to the entire subscription.\n126:   absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>\n127:   findAdditions(const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& newly_added_to_watch, Watch* watch);\n128: \n129:   // Given a list of names that an individual watch no longer cares about, returns those names that\n130:   // in fact the entire subscription no longer cares about.\n131:   absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>\n132:   findRemovals(const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& newly_removed_from_watch, Watch* watch);\n133: \n134:   // Returns the union of watch_interest_[resource_name] and wildcard_watches_.\n135:   absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*> watchesInterestedIn(const std::string& resource_name);\n136: \n137:   absl::flat_hash_set<std::unique_ptr<Watch>> watches_;\n138: \n139:   // Watches whose interest set is currently empty, which is interpreted as \"everything\".\n140:   absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*> wildcard_watches_;\n141: \n142:   // Watches that have been removed inside the call stack of the WatchMap's onConfigUpdate(). This\n143:   // can happen when a watch's onConfigUpdate() results in another watch being removed via\n144:   // removeWatch().\n145:   std::unique_ptr<absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*>> deferred_removed_during_update_;\n146: \n147:   // Maps a resource name to the set of watches interested in that resource. Has two purposes:\n148:   // 1) Acts as a reference count; no watches care anymore ==> the resource can be removed.\n149:   // 2) Enables efficient lookup of all interested watches when a resource has been updated.\n150:   absl::flat_hash_map<std::string, absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*>> watch_interest_;\n151: \n152:   const bool use_namespace_matching_;\n153:   const std::string type_url_;\n154:   CustomConfigValidators* config_validators_;\n155:   EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache_;\n156: };\n157: \n158: } // namespace Config\n159: } // namespace Envoy\n160: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/envoyproxy/envoy@97d755340d57ce4726ab296f1d5a022652948eec/-/blob/source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.h"}}}

These invocations\\n30:  * will be followed by the GrpcMuxFailover calling the GrpcStreamCallbacks on the GrpcMux\\n31:  * object that initialized it.\\n32:  *\\n33:  * To simplify the state-machine, Envoy can be in one of the mutually exclusive states:\\n34:  *   ConnectingToPrimary - attempting to connect to the primary source.\\n35:  *   ConnectedToPrimary - after receiving a response from the primary source.\\n36:  *   ConnectingToFailover - attempting to connect to the failover source.\\n37:  *   ConnectedToFailover - after receiving a response from the failover source.\\n38:  *   None - not attempting to connect or connected to any source (e.g., upon  initialization).\\n39:  *\\n40:  * The GrpcMuxFailover attempts to establish a connection to the primary source. If a response from the failover source is received, it will be the\\n47:  * source of configuration until the connection is closed. ConnectionState::ConnectedToPrimary ||\\n100:         connection_state_ == ConnectionState::ConnectedToFailover) {\\n101:       ENVOY_LOG_MISC(trace,\\n102:                      \\\"Already connected If a response from the failover source is received, it will be the\\n47:  * source of configuration until the connection is closed. In case the failover connection is\\n48:  * closed, Envoy will attempt to connect to the primary, before retrying to connect to the failover\\n49:  * source. If the failover source is unavailable or a connection to it is closed, the\\n50:  * GrpcMuxFailover will alternate between attempts to reconnect to the primary source and the\\n51:  * failover source.\\n52:  * TODO(adisuissa): The number of consecutive failures is currently statically\\n53:  * defined, and may be converted to a config field in the future.\\n54:  */\\n55: template <class RequestType, class ResponseType>\\n56: class GrpcMuxFailover : public GrpcStreamInterface<RequestType, ResponseType>,\\n57:                         public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\\n58: public:\\n59:   static constexpr uint32_t DefaultFailoverBackoffMilliseconds = 500;\\n60: \\n61:   // A GrpcStream creator function that receives the stream callbacks and returns a\\n62:   // GrpcStream object.
